### Round 1 | planner | planner_initial

- diagnosis: Task: infer the most likely AIE mechanism label (ICT/TICT/ESIPT/neutral aromatic/unknown) for the provided C58H40N2S molecule using the prepared structure context plus quick first-round analyses.

Top1 vs Top2: Top1 is TICT (working hypothesis) and Top2 is neutral aromatic (RIM-dominated without explicit CT/TICT). The molecule is a large polyaryl/oligostyryl system with ~10 rotatable bonds and many phenyl rings; this creates multiple torsional degrees of freedom that can enable twisted excited-state conformations that are quenched in solution and rigidified in aggregates (supporting TICT-suppression/RIM). However, the scaffold is also largely hydrocarbon and fairly planar by proxy, with only one heteroaromatic N2S-containing fused motif; that makes it plausible that AIE is driven more generally by restriction of intramolecular rotations in a neutral aromatic system rather than a distinct TICT state.

Why top1 is uncertain: we do not yet know whether the lowest bright S1 has strong charge-transfer character and whether a twisted minimum exists/competes (key for distinguishing TICT from generic neutral-aromatic RIM). Evidence to separate TICT from neutral aromatic later: (i) computed excited-state density difference / transition dipole localization and change with torsion; (ii) sensitivity of S1 energy/oscillator strength to torsional scans; (iii) predicted large dipole change (ICT/TICT) vs small (neutral aromatic).

Context availability: shared prepared 3D structure is ready (101 atoms; 10 conformers; rotatable bonds=10; aromatic rings=10; planarity_proxy~0.97).

Agent realism: Macro can do mechanism-level pattern recognition from structure proxies (rotors, donor/acceptor motifs, planarity, likely RIM) but cannot prove excited-state topology. Microscopic can run low-cost bounded computations (aTB S0 optimization and a small set of vertical excitations / limited torsion probes) but should not attempt exhaustive DFT for this large system in round 1. First round should gather both: macro chemical-structure priors plus microscopic quick signals of CT/twist sensitivity.

- action: macro_and_microscopic

- confidence: 0.48

- task_instruction: Run first-round Macro and Microscopic evidence gathering to discriminate TICT vs neutral aromatic (RIM) and flag whether ICT character is likely.

- agent_task_instructions: {"macro": "Assess macro-level structural evidence relevant to the current working hypothesis 'TICT'. Reuse the shared prepared structure context when available, summarize low-cost structural indicators only, and stay within current macro capability. Hypothesis uncertainty to keep in mind: TICT is favored due to multiple rotatable aryl linkages enabling twisted excited states that can be suppressed by aggregation, but the molecule’s largely hydrocarbon, highly conjugated character could instead indicate a neutral-aromatic RIM AIE without distinct TICT; distinguishing requires quick excited-state/dihedral sensitivity evidence.", "microscopic": "Run the first-round low-cost S0/S1 microscopic baseline task for the current working hypothesis 'TICT'. Reuse the shared prepared structure context when available. Prioritize semi-empirical or otherwise low-cost bounded evidence collection, not heavy exhaustive geometry optimization. Report local microscopic results only, and do not attempt mechanism discrimination beyond current microscopic capability. Capability note: Macro: can interpret structural motifs and AIE heuristics (rotors, sterics, donor/acceptor patterns) and propose discriminative experimental signatures, but cannot confirm excited-state minima. Microscopic: can run bounded aTB S0 optimization and limited vertical excitations/torsion probes on 1–2 dihedrals; it cannot in round 1 map full excited-state PES, perform exhaustive conformer searches, or do high-level TDDFT across many conformers for this 101-atom system."}

- hypothesis_uncertainty_note: TICT is favored due to multiple rotatable aryl linkages enabling twisted excited states that can be suppressed by aggregation, but the molecule’s largely hydrocarbon, highly conjugated character could instead indicate a neutral-aromatic RIM AIE without distinct TICT; distinguishing requires quick excited-state/dihedral sensitivity evidence.

### Round 1 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=neutral aromatic (strengthened). Top2=TICT (weakened relative to prior). Latest evidence shifts weight toward neutral aromatic because macro descriptors show a highly polyaryl, low-hetero, planar-leaning scaffold (hetero_atom_count=3; planarity_proxy=0.974), which is more typical of RIM-driven AIE without strong CT. Microscopic baseline shows the lowest excited state is already bright (E1=3.0585 eV, f1=1.0298), which is less characteristic of a lowest CT/TICT state (often weakly allowed) and more consistent with π–π* aromatic excitation. TICT remains plausible due to multiple rotors (rotatable_bond_count=10; conformer_dispersion_proxy=1.0), but lacks clear D–A separation and CT signatures so far. Key remaining discriminator (neutral aromatic vs TICT): whether twisting of a specific aryl–aryl/exocyclic linkage produces a CT-like state (drop in oscillator strength, increase in dipole/charge separation) and whether emission properties show strong solvent polarity/viscosity dependence consistent with TICT. Reasoning summary: From the shared structure context, the molecule is a large, highly aromatic polyaryl system (10 aromatic rings; 101 atoms) with only one small heteroaromatic unit (3 hetero atoms total, consistent with a single NSN-containing ring). The rotatable bond count is moderate (10) and torsion candidates match this, indicating multiple aryl–aryl/exocyclic C=C linkages that can twist. However, the planarity_proxy is high (~0.97), suggesting the selected conformer is largely coplanar/extended conjugation rather than strongly twisted at rest; this weakens direct structural support for a strongly twisted ICT ground-state geometry, though TICT concerns excited-state twisting specifically. The donor–acceptor partition proxy (~0.5) and very low hetero content argue against a pronounced intramolecular donor–acceptor architecture typical of strong TICT emitters; instead, the structure looks predominantly neutral/hydrocarbon conjugation with rotatable phenyl substituents—structurally compatible with RIM-type AIE as well. Conformer_dispersion_proxy at 1.0 (with 10 conformers prepared) indicates nontrivial conformational variability is present in low-cost sampling, consistent with torsional flexibility that could enable excited-state twisting, but the available proxies cannot confirm a charge-transfer character or identify a specific D–A dihedral controlling TICT.
Capability limit note: This macro pass is limited to deterministic topology and provided geometry proxies from the prepared structure; it cannot compute excited-state charge transfer, identify TICT minima, or model aggregation/packing effects. Conclusions are therefore structural plausibility indicators only, not mechanism determination.

This directly challenges the key TICT signature (twist-induced formation of a low-lying dark state). ICT remains plausible only as a minor component because the molecule contains an NSN heteroaromatic unit, but torsion does not reveal CT-like darkening in the lowest state. Key remaining discriminator (neutral aromatic vs TICT): whether any other untested torsion coordinate and/or solvent polarity can stabilize a dark CT state below the bright state (requires either broader torsion coverage or environment-sensitive evidence). ### Round 6 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=neutral aromatic (strengthened) vs Top2=ICT (promoted above TICT). Latest evidence strengthens Top1 because a third independent torsion probe (dih_13_14_15_16, 0° vs 90°) with expanded S1–S7 window still reports lowest_state_is_bright (e.g., S1 f~0.285 at 0° and ~0.511 at 90°) with no indication of a lower dark state displacing the bright state. This directly weakens TICT because the expected twist-induced dark/CT state reordering is not observed even under large torsional decoupling across multiple high-relevance dihedrals. ICT remains plausible as a runner-up (NSN unit) but is constrained by the consistently bright lowest excitation. Key remaining discriminator between neutral aromatic and the remaining challengers (ICT/TICT) is evidence of environment- or relaxation-driven CT stabilization (e.g., strong solvatochromism, excited-state optimized CT minima), which is not captured by current vertical-only snapshots. Verifier supplementation remains missing (403 region restriction). Closure justification is now close to sufficient internally for neutral aromatic vs TICT (3 torsions, up to S1–S7), but still lacks excited-state relaxation/solvent sensitivity confirmation. The best next action is a minimal additional internal discriminator that targets CT character directly (within available tools), rather than another similar torsion scan.

### Round 7 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=neutral aromatic (strengthened) and Top2=ICT (runner-up; replaces TICT). Latest evidence strengthens neutral aromatic because (i) three independent NSN-adjacent/high-relevance dihedral twists (0° vs 90°) show lowest_state_is_bright with substantial oscillator strength and no dark-state reordering up to S1–S7, and (ii) baseline vertical S1 is very bright (f~1.03). This strongly weakens TICT as a challenger (no twist-induced dark/CT lowest-state signature). ICT remains the primary challenger only because an NSN acceptor fragment exists, but the key remaining discriminator between neutral aromatic vs ICT is direct CT-character evidence (excited-state dipole/charge-separation proxies or clear solvatochromism/viscosity dependence), which is currently missing/unsupported by outputs. Verifier supplementation remains missing (403 blocked). Closure justification vs TICT is now close to sufficient internally; the best next action is to run a bounded internal task to extract any available CT proxies (S0 dipole already available) or orbital localization descriptors to discriminate neutral aromatic vs ICT without relying on the blocked verifier.
